Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Kafalah for A'yan Madhmun bi Nafsihi: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Classifies a'yan and rules on kafalah with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a'yan into the three categories (madhmun bi nafsihi, madhmun bighayrihi, ghayr madhmun), state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah for each, and explain the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Kafalah for an item is valid only if the principal can be demanded to return it or pay its value.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi classification of corporeal objects (a'yan) for the purpose of kafalah (suretyship). The key distinction is whether an item is 'guaranteed in itself' (madhmun bi nafsihi) or guaranteed by another obligation (madhmun bighayrihi). This classification determines whether kafalah for the item itself is valid. The Hanafi position is opposed by Imam al-Shafi'i, who rejects kafalah for any corporeal object. We will walk through the arguments and understand why the Hanafi view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Classify a'yan
Identify the three categories: (i) madhmun bi nafsihi (guaranteed in itself — e.g., sold item in void sale, usurped item), (ii) madhmun bighayrihi (guaranteed by another — e.g., sold item in valid sale, pawned item), (iii) ghayr madhmun (not guaranteed — e.g., deposit, loan).
Focus on the definition: for madhmun bi nafsihi, destruction triggers a value obligation; for madhmun bighayrihi, the item is secured for another debt.
2
State Hanafi ruling on kafalah for the item itself
Hanafis rule that kafalah for the item itself (dhat) is valid only for madhmun bi nafsihi; for the other two categories, it is invalid by consensus with Shafi'is (except the dispute on madhmun bi nafsihi).
This ruling is based on the principle that kafalah joins liability in demand; demand requires the item to be guaranteed on the principal.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that kafalah is for debts, not corporeal objects, and that the surety must be able to deliver the exact item, which is not possible for specific a'yan.
Shafi'i defines kafalah as transferring the obligation to the surety, requiring ability to deliver the very item.
4
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafis respond that kafalah is joining one liability to another in demand (mutalaba), not transfer of ownership. The surety can be demanded to produce the item or its value. The condition of ability to deliver is not absolute; it suffices that the principal can be demanded. Since for madhmun bi nafsihi the principal is liable, the surety can also be liable.
Key: the Hanafi definition allows kafalah for items where the principal can be demanded to either return the item or pay the value.
5
Apply to kafalah for delivery (taslim)
Distinguish the second type: kafalah for delivery is valid if the item is wajib al-taslim on the principal (e.g., seller delivering sold item, pledgee returning pawn after debt). It is invalid for items where the principal is not obligated to deliver (e.g., deposits, mudaraba capital).
This reinforces the principle: kafalah mirrors the principal's liability.

كتاب الكفاله

اعيان مضمونہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں (1) مضمون بنفسہ، مثلاً بیع فاسد کی صورت میں مشتری کے قبضہ میں مبیع اور وہ چیز جس پر خریدنے کے لیے قبضہ کیا گیا ہے یعنی جس شخص کا ارادہ خریدنے کا ہے اس نے بائع سے اجازت لے کر ایک چیز پر قبضہ کیا ہے جس کے دام دونوں نے بیان کر دیئے ہیں اور مشتری نے کہا کہ اگر گھر والوں کو پسند آگئی تو میں تجھ سے خرید لوں گا پس یہ چیز مقبوض علی سوم الشراء کہلائے گی اور غاصب کے قبضہ میں شیء مغصوب مضمون بنفسہ ہیں۔ چنانچہ مذکورہ صورتوں میں شئی کے موجود ہونے کی صورت میں اس کا واپس کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے اور ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت جو اس کے قائم مقام ہے واجب ہوتی ہے۔
(2) مضمون بغیرہ مثلاً بیع صحیح کی صورت میں مبیع بائع کے قبضہ میں کہ وہ ثمن کے عوض مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی بائع مبیع کا ضامن ثمن کے عوض ہوتا ہے اور جیسے شیء مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ میں کہ وہ قرضہ کے عوض مضمون ہوتی ہے، چنانچہ اگر شیء مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو گئی تو اس کے بدلے میں راہن کے ذمہ سے اس کی قیمت کے بقدر قرضہ ساقط ہو جائے گا حاصل یہ کہ بیع صحیح میں مبیع اور شیء مرہون اپنی ذات کے علاوہ دوسری چیز یعنی ثمن اور قرضہ کے عوض مضمون ہوتی ہیں اب یہ اعیان مضمونہ ہوں یا غیر مضمونہ ہوں اور مضمون بنفسہا ہوں یا مضمون بغیر ہا ہوں ان تمام کے کفالہ کی دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو ان کی ذات کا کفیل ہو گا اور یا محض ان کو سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہوگا۔ اگر اول ہے یعنی اعیان کی ذوات کا کفیل ہوا ہے تو اعیان غیر مضمونہ یعنی مال ودیعت اور شیء مستعار وغیرہ اور اعیان مضمونہ بغیر ہا یعنی مبیع اور شیء مرہون کا کفالہ شوافع اور احناف دونوں کے نزدیک درست نہیں ہے اور اعیان مضمونہ بنفسہا یعنی بیع فاسد میں مبیع جس پر مشتری کا قبضہ ہے اور مقبوض علی سوم الشراء اور شیء مغصوب کا کفالہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اعیان مضمونہ بنفسہا کا کفالہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک مطلقاً اعیان کا کفالہ اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک کفالہ کا موجب اصل دین کو اپنے اوپر لازم کرنا ہے گویا کفالہ کا محل دیون ہیں نہ کہ اعیان پس جب کفالہ کا محل دیون ہیں نہ کہ اعیان تو اعیان کا کفالہ کس طرح درست ہوگا نیز صحت کفالہ کی شرط یہ ہے کہ کفیل اپنے پاس سے مملوک بہ ادا کرنے پر قادر ہو اور یہ شرط دیون کے اندر تو متصور ہو سکتی ہے لیکن اعیان کے اندر متصور نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اس لئے بھی اعیان کا کفالہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ کفالہ ایک ذمہ کو دوسرے ذمہ کے ساتھ مطالبہ میں ملانے کا نام ہے اور مطالبہ تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ مطلوب یعنی وہ چیز جس کا مطالبہ کیا جائے گا اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ پر مضمون ہو حالانکہ امانتیں یعنی اعیان غیر مضمونہ مضمون نہیں ہوتیں چنانچہ اگر مال امانت یا مال مستعار وغیرہ قابض یعنی اصیل کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں آتا اور اسی طرح مضمون بغیر یعنی بیع جو مضمون بالثمن ہوتی ہے اور شیء مرہون جو مضمون بالدین ہوتی ہے یہ اصیل پر مضمون نہیں ہوتیں۔ چنانچہ اگر مبیع بائع کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئی تو ثمن ساقط ہو جائے گا اور عقد فسخ ہو جائے گا۔ اور شیء مرہون اگر مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہوگئی تو مرتہن اپنا قرضہ وصول کرنے والا شمار ہوگا اور بائع اور مرتہن پر مطالبہ لازم نہ ہوگا اور جب خود ان پر مطالبہ لازم نہیں ہوا تو کفیل پر مطالبہ کیسے لازم ہوگا۔ اور جب کفیل پر مطالبہ لازم نہیں ہو سکتا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں کفالہ کس طرح درست ہوگا اعیان مضمونہ بنفسہا میں چونکہ اصیل پر مطالبہ لازم ہوتا ہے چنانچہ بیع فاسد کی صورت میں مشتری سے عین مبیع واپس کرنے کا مطالبہ ہوگا اور اگر عین مبیع ہلاک ہو گئی تو اس کی قیمت کا مطالبہ ہو گا اسی طرح اگر مقبوض علی سوم الشراء اور شیء مغصوب ہلاک ہو گئی تو اس کی قیمت کا مطالبہ ہو گا بشرطیکہ وہ شیء ذوات القیم میں سے ہو پس جب اعیان مضمونہ بنفسہا کا مطالبہ اصیل سے ہو سکتا ہے تو ان کا مطالبہ کفیل سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور جب کفیل سے ان کا مطالبہ کیا جا سکتا ہے تو ان کا کفالہ بھی جائز ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ اعیان مضمونہ بنفسہا کا کفالہ جائز ہے اور اعیان مضمونہ بغیر ہا اور اعیان غیر مضمونہ کا کفالہ نا جائز ہے۔
اس تمہید کے بعد دلیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ بائع کی طرف سے مبیع کا کفیل ہونا بایں طور کہ کفیل مشتری سے کہے کہ اگر مبیع بائع کے پاس ہلاک ہوگئی تو اس کے بدل کا ذمہ دار میں ہوں ناجائز اس لئے ہے کہ مبیع ایسا عین ہے جو مضمون بغیرہ ہے یعنی ثمن کے عوض بائع کی ضمانت میں ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ ہمارے نزدیک اعیان مضمونہ بغیر ہا کا کفالہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بائع کی طرف مشتری کے لئے مبیع کا کفیل ہونا بھی درست نہ ہوگا اور اگر ثانی ہے یعنی اعیان مذکورہ کو سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہوا اور وہ اعیان واجب التسلیم بھی ہوں مثلاً ایک آدمی بیع صحیح میں مشتری کو بائع کی طرف سے مبیع سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہو گیا یا مرتہن کے مال قرض پر قبضہ کے بعد ایک آدمی شیء مرہونہ راہن کی طرف سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہو گیا یا شیء مستاجر کو اجرت پر لینے والے کی طرف سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہو گیا تو یہ کفالہ جائز ہے پس اگر مبیع بائع کے پاس ہلاک ہوگئی تو کفیل پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ عقد بیع ہی فسخ ہوگیا البتہ بائع پر ثمن واپس کرنا واجب ہو گا اس طرح قرضہ وصول کرنے کے بعد اگر شیء مرہون مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئی تو کفیل پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا البتہ مرتہن پر قرضہ کے مالک کا واپس کرنا واجب ہو گا بشرطیکہ قرضہ کا مال شیء مرہونہ کی مالیت کے برابر ہو یا شیء مرہونہ کی مالیت قرضہ سے زائد ہو کیونکہ شیء مرہونہ میں قرضہ کی مقدار سے جو حصہ زائد ہے وہ مرتہن کے پاس امانت ہے اور امانت کا کوئی ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے شیء مرہونہ کے حصہ زائد کا کوئی ضمان مرتہن پر واجب نہ ہوگا اسی طرح اگر شیء مستاجر اجرت پر دینے والے کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئی تو کفیل پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں عقد اجارہ ہی فسخ ہو گیا ہے بہر حال اعیان اگر واجب التسلیم ہوں تو ان کو سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہونا جائز ہے کیونکہ کفیل نے ایسے فعل کا التزام کیا ہے جو خود اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے چنانچہ بائع پر مبیع کا سپرد کرنا اور مرتہن پر اپنا قرضہ وصول کرنے کے بعد شیء مرہونہ کو سپرد کرنا اور اجرت پر دینے والے پر شیء مستاجر کو سپرد کرنا واجب تھا پس کفیل نے اس فعل کا التزام کیا ہے جو اس کے مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے اور جو فعل مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہو اس کا کفیل ہونا چونکہ جائز ہے اس لئے واجب التسلیم اعیان کے سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہونا بھی جائز ہوگا اور اگر اعیان واجب التسلیم نہ ہوں یعنی ان کا سپرد کرنا خود اصیل پر واجب نہ ہوگا جیسے مال امانت، مال مضاربت اور مال شرکت تو ان کو سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہونا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ مال امانت، مال مضاربت اور مال شرکت میں طلب کے وقت یہ واجب ہے کہ امین، صاحب مال کو، مضارب، رب المال کو اور ایک شریک اپنے ساتھی کو قبضہ کرنے سے نہ روکے اور امین، مضارب اور شریک پر خود سپرد کرنا واجب نہیں ہے پس جب نہیں ہے تو کفیل پر سپرد کرنا کس طرح واجب ہوگا اور جب کفیل پر ان اموال کا سپرد کرنا واجب نہیں ہوا تو ان اموال کا کفالہ بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Kafalah. There are two types of guaranteed corporeal objects: (1) Guaranteed in themselves, e.g., in a void sale, the sold item in the buyer's possession, and an item taken with permission to purchase (maqbud 'ala som al-shira'), and a usurped item in the usurper's possession. In these cases, if the item exists, its return is obligatory; if destroyed, its value is obligatory. (2) Guaranteed by another, e.g., in a valid sale, the sold item in the seller's possession is guaranteed in exchange for the price; similarly, a pawned item in the pledgee's possession is guaranteed in exchange for the debt. If the pawned item is destroyed, the debt is reduced by its value. Now, for all these types, kafalah is either for the items themselves or for their delivery. If for the items themselves, then kafalah for non-guaranteed items (like deposits and loans) and for items guaranteed by another (like sold item in valid sale and pawned item) is impermissible according to both Shafi'is and Hanafis. Kafalah for items guaranteed in themselves (like sold item in void sale, maqbud 'ala som al-shira', and usurped item) is permissible according to us, though Imam Shafi'i considers it impermissible. Shafi'i argues that kafalah is essentially undertaking a debt, not a corporeal object; also the surety must be able to deliver what is owned, which is possible for debts but not for specific objects. Our response: Kafalah is joining one liability to another in demand. Demand requires that the demanded thing be guaranteed on the principal. Non-guaranteed items and items guaranteed by another are not guaranteed on the principal, so demand cannot be made on the surety. But for items guaranteed in themselves, demand can be made on the principal, so it can also be made on the surety; hence kafalah for them is valid. Therefore, kafalah for items guaranteed in themselves is valid, and for items guaranteed by another and non-guaranteed items is invalid. After this premise, the summary of proof: Kafalah by the seller for the sold item (saying to buyer: if it is destroyed, I am responsible) is invalid because the sold item is guaranteed by another (by the price). As for kafalah for delivery, if the items are obligatory to deliver (e.g., sold item in valid sale, pawned item after debt collection, leased item), then kafalah for delivery is valid because the surety undertakes an act that is obligatory on the principal. If the items are not obligatory to deliver (like deposits, mudaraba capital, partnership property), then kafalah for delivery is invalid because the principal is not obligated to deliver them himself.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Kafalah of Ashraf al-Hidayah is a detailed legal analysis (inter-madhhab dispute) concerning the validity of kafalah (suretyship) for different categories of corporeal objects (a'yan). The author begins by classifying a'yan into two types: (1) madhmun bi nafsihi (guaranteed in themselves) — items that if destroyed, their value is owed by the possessor, such as a sold item in a void sale (bay' fasid), an item taken with permission to purchase (maqbud 'ala som al-shira'), or a usurped item. (2) madhmun bighayrihi (guaranteed by something else) — items that are guaranteed not by themselves but in exchange for another obligation, such as a sold item in a valid sale (guaranteed for the price) or a pawned item (guaranteed for the debt). There are also non-guaranteed items (ghayr madhmun) like deposits and loans. The author then presents the ruling on kafalah: for kafalah of the item itself (dhat), it is valid only for items guaranteed in themselves; for items guaranteed by another and non-guaranteed items, it is invalid according to both Hanafis and Shafi'is. Then the dispute with Imam Shafi'i is presented: Shafi'i considers kafalah for items guaranteed in themselves also invalid. His reasoning: kafalah is essentially for debts, not corporeal objects; the surety must be able to deliver what is owned, which is possible for debts but not for specific items. The Hanafi response: kafalah is about joining one liability to another in terms of demand (mutalaba). Demand is only meaningful if the demanded thing is guaranteed on the principal. For items guaranteed in themselves, the principal is liable to return the item or pay its value; hence demand can be made on him. Therefore, the surety can also be demanded. For items guaranteed by another, the principal (seller or pledgee) is not liable for the item itself — if it is destroyed, the contract is rescinded or the debt is reduced — so no demand can be made on the principal, and thus not on the surety. The passage then covers a second type of kafalah: kafalah for delivery (taslim). This is valid if the item is wajib al-taslim (obligatory to deliver) on the principal, such as a seller delivering the sold item in a valid sale, a pledgee returning the pawned item after receiving the debt, or a lessor delivering the leased item. If the principal is not obligated to deliver the item himself (e.g., deposits, mudaraba capital, partnership property), then kafalah for delivery is invalid because the surety cannot be obligated to do what is not obligatory on the principal. The key principle: kafalah is valid only where the principal (asil) can be demanded to fulfill the obligation. This classification ensures that the surety’s obligation mirrors the principal’s liability.

Key Terms
مضمون بنفسہ (madhmun bi nafsihi): An item that is guaranteed in itself, i.e., if it is destroyed, its possessor must pay its value irrespective of any other obligation.
مضمون بغیرہ (madhmun bighayrihi): An item that is guaranteed not by itself but in exchange for another obligation (e.g., price or debt).
کفالہ (kafalah): A contract where a person (kafil) joins his liability to that of another (asil) in terms of demand for a specific obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, kafalah for which of the following is valid?
A) A deposit (wadi'ah) held by the depositee
B) A sold item in a valid sale still with the seller
C) A usurped item (maghsab) in the usurper's possession
D) A pawned item (mahrun) in the pledgee's possession

Key Takeaway
Kafalah for an item's own return is valid only if the item is madhmun bi nafsihi, because the principal can be demanded to return it or pay its value.

Kafalah for Guaranteed and Non-Guaranteed Assets
Establishes rulings for kafalah of a'yan madmunah and ghayr madmunah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha, bi-ghayriha, and ghayr madmunah, and state the ruling for kafalah for each, including the proof and the rule for delivery guarantees.

Core Idea
A guarantee is valid only for assets that are personally guaranteed; others are not.

This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on kafalah (guarantee) for different types of assets. It establishes a general principle: valid guarantees are restricted to assets that are 'guaranteed in themselves' (a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha), while guarantees for assets 'guaranteed by something else' or 'non-guaranteed' are invalid. The text further applies this to delivery guarantees, distinguishing between items that are wajib al-taslim (obligatory to deliver) and those that are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of assets
Find in the text the three types: a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha (guaranteed in themselves), a'yan madmunah bi-ghayriha (guaranteed by something else), and a'yan ghayr madmunah (non-guaranteed). Note examples of each.
Examples: usurped item (first type), sold item in a valid sale (second type), trust property (third type).
2
State the general principle of validity
The author states: if a claim can be made against the principal (asil) for the asset, then it can also be made against the guarantor; therefore kafalah is valid. Conversely, if no such claim exists, kafalah is invalid.
This principle underlies the entire ruling.
3
Analyze the proof for each category
For a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha: loss creates direct liability, so claim is possible. For a'yan madmunah bi-ghayriha: the asset is guaranteed by something else (e.g., price); no direct liability on the holder, so kafalah invalid. For ghayr madmunah: no liability at all.
The proof uses analogy (qiyas) from existing rulings.
4
Apply the rule to delivery guarantees
The text distinguishes: guaranteeing delivery (taslim) of an item that is wajib al-taslim (obligatory to deliver) is valid because the principal is obligated to deliver. For items not wajib al-taslim (e.g., trusts), delivery is not obligatory, so guarantee invalid.
Delivery guarantee is about the act of delivery, not the asset itself.
5
Work through the practical examples
The passage gives examples: valid sale delivery guarantee, mortgage return guarantee, hire return guarantee. In each, if the item perishes, the guarantor is not liable for value because the contract dissolves; the principal bears loss.
This shows the practical consequence of the rule.

عنہ پر واجب ہو اس کا کفیل ہونا چونکہ جائز ہے اس لئے واجب التسلیم اعیان کے سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہونا بھی جائز ہوگا اور اگر اعیان واجب التسلیم نہ ہوں یعنی ان کا سپر د کرنا خود اصیل پر واجب نہ ہوگا جیسے مال امانت، مال مضاربت اور مال شرکت تو ان کو سپرد کرنے کا نفیل ہونا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ مال امانت، مال مضاربت اور مال شرکت میں طلب کے وقت یہ واجب ہے کہ امین ، صاحب مال کو ، مضارب ، رب المال کو اور ایک شریک اپنے ساتھی کو قبضہ کرنے سے نہ روکے اور امین ، مضارب اور شریک پر خود سپرد کرنا واجب نہیں ہے پس جب نہیں ہے تو کفیل پر سپرد کرنا کس طرح واجب ہوگا اور جب کفیل پر ان اموال کا سپر د کرنا واجب نہیں ہوا تو ان اموال کا کفالہ بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔
A claim becomes necessary. For example, in the case of an invalid sale, the claim from the buyer is for return of the specific sold item, and if the specific sold item perishes, then a claim for its price. Similarly, if something received on a faulty purchase or a usurped item perishes, then a claim for its price, provided that item is among those with value. So when claims against the principal (asil) are possible for the very 'ayn (specific items) that are guaranteed in themselves (a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha), then claims against the guarantor (kafil) are also possible. And when claims against the guarantor are possible, then kafalah for them is valid. Thus it is established that kafalah for a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha is valid, and kafalah for a'yan madmunah bi-ghayriha (guaranteed by something else) and a'yan ghayr madmunah (non-guaranteed) is not valid. After this introduction, the summary of the proof is that being a guarantor from the seller's side for the sold item, such that the guarantor says to the buyer: 'If the sold item perishes with the seller, I am responsible for its replacement,' is invalid because the sold item is an 'ayn that is madmun bi-ghayrihi (guaranteed by something else, i.e., by the price). And it has passed before that in our view kafalah for a'yan madmunah bi-ghayriha is not valid. So being a guarantor for the sold item from the seller's side for the buyer is also not valid. And if it is the second type, i.e., one becomes a guarantor for delivering the said items, and those items are wajib al-taslim (obligatory to deliver), for example a person becomes a guarantor for delivering the sold item from the seller to the buyer in a valid sale, or after the mortgagee has taken possession of the collateral on a loan, a person becomes a guarantor for delivering the mortgaged item to the mortgagor, or a person becomes a guarantor for delivering the hired item to the lessor, then this kafalah is valid. If the sold item perishes with the seller, then nothing becomes obligatory on the guarantor, because the sale contract is dissolved; however, the seller is obligated to return the price. Similarly, after receiving the loan, if the mortgaged item perishes with the mortgagee, then nothing is obligatory on the guarantor; however, the mortgagee is obligated to return the loan amount, provided the loan amount equals the value of the mortgaged item or is less than it, because the portion of the mortgaged item exceeding the loan amount is an amanah (trust) with the mortgagee, and no guarantee is obligatory for an amanah. So no guarantee is obligatory on the mortgagee for the excess portion. Similarly, if the hired item perishes with the lessor, then nothing is obligatory on the guarantor, because in this case the lease contract is dissolved. In any case, if the items are wajib al-taslim, then being a guarantor for delivering them is valid, because the guarantor has undertaken an act that is obligatory on the principal (asil, i.e., the one on whose behalf the guarantee is given). Thus, the seller was obligated to deliver the sold item, the mortgagee after receiving his loan was obligated to deliver the mortgaged item, and the lessor was obligated to deliver the hired item. So the guarantor has undertaken an act that is obligatory on his principal, and since being a guarantor for what is obligatory on the principal is valid, therefore being a guarantor for delivering wajib al-taslim items is also valid. And if the items are not wajib al-taslim, i.e., their delivery is not obligatory on the principal himself, like property held as amanah, mudarabah property, and partnership property, then being a guarantor for delivering them is not valid, because in amanah property, mudarabah property, and partnership property, at the time of demand it is obligatory that the trustee not prevent the owner from taking possession, the mudarib not prevent the rabb al-mal, and one partner not prevent the other from taking possession; it is not obligatory on the trustee, mudarib, and partner to themselves deliver. So when it is not obligatory, how can it become obligatory on the guarantor? And when delivering these assets is not obligatory on the guarantor, then kafalah for these assets is also not valid.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof regarding the validity of kafalah (guarantee) for different types of assets. The author first establishes a general principle: kafalah is valid for assets that are 'guaranteed in themselves' (a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha), meaning assets whose loss would normally result in liability for their owner. For example, if someone buys an item in an invalid sale or usurps something, those items are guaranteed; the owner can claim them or their value. Since such claims can be made directly from the principal (asil), they can also be made from the guarantor, so taking a guarantee for such items is valid. Conversely, kafalah is invalid for assets 'guaranteed by something else' (a'yan madmunah bi-ghayriha), like the sold item in a valid sale which is guaranteed by the price, and for non-guaranteed assets (a'yan ghayr madmunah) like mere trusts. The text then elaborates by comparing the sale case: if a person guarantees to the buyer that if the sold item perishes with the seller, he will compensate, this is invalid because the sold item is already guaranteed by the price; it is not a direct liability on the seller in the sense of a standalone guarantee. The second part discusses kafalah for the delivery (taslim) of items that are wajib al-taslim (obligatory to deliver), such as delivering the sold item in a valid sale, returning a mortgaged item after repayment, or returning a hired item after the lease. Since the principal is obligated to deliver, the guarantor can validly undertake that obligation. If the item perishes, the guarantor is not liable because the contract is rescinded; the principal bears the loss. In contrast, for items that are not wajib al-taslim, like trusts (amana, mudaraba, partnership), the principal is only obligated to allow possession, not to deliver; thus the guarantor cannot validly guarantee delivery. The passage demonstrates careful Hanafi reasoning distinguishing between types of guarantees based on the nature of the obligation and the underlying liability.

Key Terms
عین مضمونہ بنفسہا (‘ayn madmūnah bi-nafsihā): An asset that is itself guaranteed, meaning its loss would normally create a liability for the holder (e.g., a usurped item or item from an invalid sale).
عین مضمونہ بغیرہا (‘ayn madmūnah bi-ghayrihā): An asset that is guaranteed by something else, e.g., the sold item in a valid sale is guaranteed by the price; it is not directly guaranteed in itself.
واجب التسلیم (wājib al-taslīm): An asset that must be delivered as an obligation arising from a contract (e.g., sold item, mortgaged item after repayment, hired item after lease).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, kafalah for which type of asset is valid?
A) A'yan madmunah bi-ghayriha (assets guaranteed by something else)
B) A'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha (assets guaranteed in themselves)
C) A'yan ghayr madmunah (non-guaranteed assets)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Kafalah is valid only for assets that are personally guaranteed (a'yan madmunah bi-nafsiha) or for delivery of items that are wajib al-taslim; otherwise it is invalid.

Kafalah for Carrying and Service: The Impact of Specification
Explains validity of kafalah for loading and service based on specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah for carrying on a hired animal and service of a hired slave, and explain why specification affects validity.

Core Idea
Kafalah is invalid if the guarantor cannot perform the specific act—capability (qudra) is a condition.

This passage rules on whether a guarantor can validly guarantee the carrying of goods on a hired animal or the service of a hired slave. The key distinction is whether the animal or slave is specified or unspecified. Understanding this clarifies the Hanafi principle that the guarantor must be capable of performing the guaranteed act, a condition rooted in the nature of kafalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two distinct situations: hiring an animal for carrying and hiring a slave for service. For each, there are two subcases based on whether the animal/slave is specified or unspecified.
Each scenario is an example of ijarah (hire) with a kafalah for the performance of an act.
2
Determine the ruling for each subcase
When the animal/slave is specified, kafalah is invalid; when unspecified, it is valid. The reason given is the guarantor's incapacity ('ajz) in the specified case.
Specification creates a unique obligation tied to a thing the guarantor cannot control.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The common thread is that a guarantor must be capable (qadir) of performing the guaranteed act. Incapacity due to lack of control or authority invalidates the contract.
This principle flows from the nature of kafalah as a binding guarantee of performance.
4
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is analogy (qiyas) to the general rule that kafalah requires qudra. The illa (effective cause) is the guarantor's inability to execute the specific act because of specification.
The proof is zanni al-thubut (based on analogy), not directly from Quran or Sunnah.

Source Text

بار برداری کے لئے جانور کرایہ پر لیا تو بار برداری کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہے
ومن استاجر دابة للحمل عليها فإن كانت بعينها لا يصح الكفالة بالحمل لأنه عاجز عنه وإن كانت بغير عينها جازت الكفالة لأنه يمكنه الحمل على دابة نفسه والحمل هو المستحق و كذا من استاجر عبدالـلـخـدمة فكفل لــــه رجـل بـخـدمته فهو باطل لــمـ بينا ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے بار برداری کے لئے جانور کرایہ پر لیا پس اگر جانور معین ہو تو بار برداری کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ کفیل اس سے عاجز ہے اور اگر جانور غیر معین ہو تو کفالہ جائز ہے کیونکہ کفیل کے لئے اپنے ذاتی جانور پر بار برداری کرنا ممکن ہے اور بار برداری ہی واجب ہوئی ہے اور اسی طرح اگر کسی نے خدمت کے واسطے ایک غلام کرایہ پر لیا پس کسی آدمی نے اسی مستاجر کے واسطے اسی غلام کی خدمت کی کفالت کی تو یہ باطل ہے اس دلیل کہ وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے ایک معینہ جانور بار برداری کے واسطے کرایہ پر لیا اور ایک آدمی مستاجر نے لئے اسی معینہ جانور پر بار برداری کا کفیل ہو گیا تو یہ بار برداری کا کفالہ جائز نہیں ہو گا دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ معینہ جانور پر بار برداری کرنے سے عاجز ہے اور کفیل جس کام کو کرنے سے عاجز ہو اس کا کفالہ چونکہ جائز نہیں ہوتا اس لئے معینہ جانور پر بار برداری کا کفالہ بھی جائز نہ ہوگا اور اگر جانور غیر معین ہوتو بار برداری کا کفالہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کفالہ سے واجب بوجوہ کا یہ پہنچانا ہے اور کفیل چونکہ اپنے ذاتی جانور پر لاد کر پہنچانے کی قدرت رکھتا ہے اس لئے یہ کفالہ درست ہو گا اسی طرح اگر کسی نے خدمت کے لئے ایک غلام کرایہ پر لیا اور دوسرا آدمی غیر معین غلام کی خدمت کا کفیل ہو گیا تو یہ کفالہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کفالہ سے خدمت واجب ہوئی ہے اور کفیل اپنے ذاتی غلام سے خدمت کرانے پر قادر ہے اور اگر معین غلام کی خدمت کا کفیل ہوا تو یہ کفالہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب کفیل کو دوسرے کے غلام پر قدرت حاصل نہیں ہے تو وہ اس معینہ غلام سے خدمت کا کفیل ہوا تو یہ کفالہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب کفیل کو دوسرے کے غلام پر قدرت حاصل نہیں ہے تو وہ اس معینہ غلام سے خدمت کرانے پر بھی قادر نہ ہو گا اور جب کفیل کو مکفول به یعنی خدمت ادا کرنے پر قدرت حاصل نہیں ہے تو اس کا کفالہ بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
If one hires an animal for carrying, then kafalah for the carrying is not valid if the animal is specific, because he is incapable of it; and if the animal is unspecified, kafalah is valid because he can load on his own animal, and carrying is what is owed. Similarly, if one hires a slave for service, and a man becomes his guarantor for his service, it is invalid for the reason we mentioned. Translation and explanation: If one hires a specific animal for carrying, and a man becomes guarantor for the hirer regarding this specific animal, this kafalah for carrying is not valid; the proof is that he is incapable of carrying on that specific animal, and when a guarantor is incapable of the act, his guarantee is invalid. If the animal is unspecified, kafalah for carrying is valid because the obligation is merely to transport, and the guarantor can transport on his own animal, so it is valid. Similarly, if one hires a slave for service, and another man becomes guarantor for the service of an unspecified slave, this kafalah is valid because the obligation is service, and the guarantor can provide service through his own slave. If he becomes guarantor for the service of a specific slave, then this kafalah is not valid because the guarantor does not have power over another's slave, and he cannot make that specific slave serve; thus he is incapable of the guaranteed act, so the guarantee is invalid.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding kafalah for an obligation to carry goods on a hired animal or to provide service from a hired slave. The core principle is that kafalah is valid only if the guarantor has the ability (qudra) to perform the guaranteed act. In the first case: if a specific animal is hired for carrying, the guarantor cannot validly guarantee the carrying because he cannot control the specific animal; his incapacity makes the guarantee invalid. But if the animal is unspecified (e.g., a general obligation to transport some goods), the guarantor can use his own animal to fulfill the obligation, so the guarantee is valid. The same logic applies to hiring a slave for service: if the slave is specified, the guarantor cannot guarantee that specific slave's service because he lacks authority over him; if the slave is unspecified, the guarantor can provide service through his own slave, so it is valid. The passage reinforces the Hanafi principle that a guarantor must be capable of fulfilling the guaranteed act; incapacity due to lack of control or authority invalidates the kafalah.

Key Terms
عاجز (‘ājiz): Incapable of performing the guaranteed act, the reason for invalidity of kafalah.
مستاجر (musta’jir): The hirer/lessee, the person who hires the animal or slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kafalah for carrying invalid when the hired animal is specified?
A) Because the animal may not be available
B) Because the guarantor is incapable of carrying on that specific animal
C) Because carrying is not a valid obligation
D) Because the hirer must do the carrying himself

Key Takeaway
For a kafalah to be valid, the guarantor must be capable of performing the guaranteed act; if the act is tied to a specific property the guarantor cannot control, the guarantee is invalid.

Kafalah and the Necessity of Acceptance in the Council: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on acceptance timing in kafalah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the requirement of acceptance in the council for kafalah, and explain the underlying legal reasoning (tamlik vs iltizam).

Core Idea
Kafalah requires both offer and acceptance in the same council according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf allows delayed acceptance.

The formation of a kafalah contract involves a dispute among the Hanafi imams about whether the creditor's acceptance must occur in the same meeting as the guarantor's offer. This lesson explores the two views and their legal rationales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the point of dispute
Identify the contract under discussion (kafalah) and the specific element in dispute: whether the creditor's acceptance must occur in the same council (majlis) as the offer.
2
State the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
State that they require acceptance in the council for validity. Understand their reasoning: kafalah involves an element of tamlik (transfer of the right of claim), making it bilateral like a sale, thus requiring mutual consent in one session.
This is the mufta bihi position in the school.
3
State the view of Abu Yusuf
State that Abu Yusuf allows delayed acceptance or subsequent ratification. Understand his reasoning: kafalah is a unilateral commitment (iltizam) by the guarantor, so the creditor's acceptance can come later, similar to his view on fuduli in marriage.
Some narrations from Abu Yusuf even dispense with explicit permission.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain the counter-argument of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: because kafalah involves tamlik, it cannot be completed with only one party's action in the council; acceptance must be immediate.
This is a key point for understanding the nature of kafalah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Identify the practical difference: if the creditor remains silent or leaves the council, the kafalah is void according to the majority, but valid upon later ratification according to Abu Yusuf. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
This difference affects real transactions.

Kafalah is concluded only by the acceptance of the creditor (makful lahu) in the council. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said it is permissible if (the creditor) is informed and then permits; and in some copies, permission is not even stipulated. The dispute applies to both kafalah bi al-nafs and kafalah bi al-mal. According to Abu Yusuf, it is an act of commitment (iltizam) so the committer acts independently; this is the basis for this narration from him. The reason for hesitation (tawaqquf) is what we mentioned regarding the fuduli in marriage. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), there is an element of tamlik (transfer of ownership) in it, namely the transfer of the right of claim; so it requires both parties, and only one part is present, so it should not depend on beyond the council. Translation and commentary: And kafalah is not valid except by the acceptance of the creditor in the council. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage records an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conclusion of a kafalah contract. The issue is whether the creditor's (makful lahu) acceptance must occur in the same council (majlis) where the guarantor makes the offer, or if it can be delayed. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that acceptance must be in the council; otherwise the contract is not valid. Their reasoning is that kafalah involves an element of tamlik (transfer of a property right)—specifically the transfer of the right to claim—so it requires an exchange of offer and acceptance similar to a sale, and thus the acceptance must be immediate in the council to avoid ambiguity. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, allowing delayed acceptance if the creditor later learns of the offer and consents. His reasoning is that kafalah is essentially a unilateral commitment (iltizam) by the guarantor; the guarantor is committing himself voluntarily, so his own act should suffice, and the creditor's acceptance can be subsequent. The text notes that some narrations from Abu Yusuf even dispense with the need for explicit permission. The phrase 'what we mentioned regarding the fuduli in marriage' refers to the analogy with a marriage contract conducted by an unauthorized agent (fuduli), where Abu Yusuf also took a more lenient position. This dispute shows the Hanafi school's internal diversity on the role of consent and timing in contracts.

Key Terms
مجلس (majlis): The session or meeting where the kafalah offer is made; the council in which acceptance must take place.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership or right; here, the transfer of the right to claim from the principal to the guarantor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is required for a kafalah contract to be valid?
A) The guarantor's offer alone
B) Acceptance by the creditor in the same council
C) The creditor's later permission
D) A written agreement

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school (majority), kafalah requires the creditor's acceptance in the same council; delayed acceptance is not sufficient.

Kafalah on Specified vs Unspecified Subjects: The Condition of Ability
Ruling on kafalah for carriage/service on specified vs unspecified subjects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah for carriage on a rented animal and distinguish between specified and unspecified subjects based on the guarantor's ability to perform.

Core Idea
Kafalah is valid only when the guarantor can perform the obligation; inability due to lack of control over a specified subject invalidates it.

This lesson examines a ruling from Kitab al-Kafalah regarding suretyship for carrying a load on a rented animal. The same principle applies analogously to hiring a slave for service. The key distinction is whether the subject (animal or slave) is specified (mu'ayyan) or unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan). This ruling hinges on the guarantor's ability (qudra) to fulfill the guaranteed obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Note the two scenarios: (1) a person rents an animal for carrying and a guarantor becomes surety for the carriage; (2) a person hires a slave for service and a guarantor becomes surety for that service.
The text treats these analogously.
2
Distinguish specified vs unspecified
In each case, the subject (animal/slave) may be specifically identified or left unspecified. The ruling changes based on this distinction.
Specified: e.g., 'this specific horse'; unspecified: e.g., 'a horse for carriage'.
3
Understand the underlying cause (illah)
The ruling depends on the guarantor's ability to perform. For a specified subject, the guarantor cannot control it (it belongs to another), so he is unable. For an unspecified subject, he can use his own property (e.g., his own animal or slave) to fulfill the obligation.
Ability to perform is a condition for valid kafalah.
4
Apply the principle
If the condition of ability is met, kafalah is valid; otherwise invalid. This principle extends to other analogous situations.
Consider modern rentals: e.g., renting a specific truck vs. a truck unspecified.

The book of Kafalah. If a person rents an animal for carrying, if it is specific, the guarantee of carrying is not valid because he is unable; if it is unspecified, the guarantee is valid because he can carry on his own animal, and the carrying is the owed obligation. Similarly, if a person hires a slave for service, and a man becomes surety for that slave's service, it is invalid for the reason we explained. Translation: And if a person rented an animal for carrying, if the animal is specific, the guarantee of carrying is not valid because the guarantor is unable; if the animal is unspecified, the guarantee is valid because the guarantor can carry on his own animal, and the carrying is the obligation. Similarly, if a person rented a slave for service and a man became surety for that slave's service, it is invalid for the reason we explained. Commentary: The case is that if a person rented a specific animal for carrying and a man became guarantor for carriage on that specific animal, the guarantee is not valid because he is unable to carry on that specific animal. If the animal is unspecified, the guarantee is valid because the obligation is to deliver the load, and the guarantor has the ability to load on his own animal. Similarly, if a slave is rented for service and another person becomes guarantor for the service of an unspecified slave, it is valid because the service is the obligation and the guarantor can have it done by his own slave. If for a specific slave, it is invalid because he has no power over another's slave and cannot make that specific slave serve.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Kafalah discusses the validity of a suretyship (kafalah) for carrying a load on a rented animal, analogous to hiring a slave for service. The ruling: if the animal is specified (mu'ayyan), the kafalah is invalid because the guarantor cannot fulfill—he cannot force the owner's specific animal to carry. If the animal is unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan), the kafalah is valid because the guarantor can use his own animal to fulfill the obligation. The same applies to a hired slave: kafalah for service of an unspecified slave is valid, but for a specific slave it is invalid because the guarantor has no control over that specific slave. The underlying principle is that kafalah requires the guarantor to be able to discharge the obligation; inability renders it invalid.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of guarantee where a person (kafil) undertakes to fulfill an obligation owed by another (makful 'anhu) to a creditor (makful lahu).
معين (mu'ayyan): Specifically identified or designated (e.g., a particular animal or slave).
غير معين (ghayr mu'ayyan): Not specifically identified; generic or unspecific (e.g., 'an animal for carriage' without specifying which animal).
عاجز ('ajiz): Unable, lacking the power or capacity to perform an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the owner did not consent

Key Takeaway
Kafalah on a specified subject is invalid due to inability; on an unspecified subject, valid because the guarantor can fulfill via his own means.

Acceptance in Session for Kafalah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains disagreement among Hanafi imams on whether creditor's acceptance in session is required

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the requirement of acceptance in the session for kafalah and explain the rationale (tamlik vs iltizam) behind each position.

Core Idea
Kafalah is a bilateral contract requiring acceptance in the session according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf sees it as a unilateral commitment or suspendable contract.

In this lesson, we examine a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the formation of the kafalah (suretyship) contract. The central question is whether the creditor's acceptance (qabul) must occur in the same session as the offer (majlis), or whether it can be given later, or even whether acceptance is needed at all. The answer hinges on how the Hanafi imams conceptualize kafalah: as a transfer of ownership (tamlik) of the right to claim, or as a commitment (iltizam) analogous to an acknowledgement or vow. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of contract theory within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed condition
From the matn, identify the specific condition debated: acceptance (qabul) of the creditor (makful lahu) in the session (majlis).
The dispute is whether this condition is necessary for validity.
2
State the mufta bihi position
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: kafalah is not valid except with acceptance in the session.
This is the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah).
3
Understand the tamlik argument
Explain the rationale: kafalah involves tamlik (transfer of ownership) of the right to claim from the kafil to the creditor. This requires both offer and acceptance, and since only the offer is present, it cannot be suspended beyond the session.
The contract is bilateral; half a contract cannot be suspended (ta'alluq).
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's two narrations
Narration 1: Kafalah is an iltizam (commitment) contract, so the kafil is independent and no acceptance is needed. Narration 2: It is a bilateral contract but acceptance can be given later, like in a fuduli marriage.
Each narration has its own evidence: iltizam analogy for the first, suspension analogy for the second.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the mufta bihi view, if the creditor does not accept in the session, kafalah is void. Under Abu Yusuf's first narration, it is valid immediately; under the second, it becomes valid upon later permission.
This affects how a kafalah contract is structured in practice.

قبول کرنا اور اس کا اجازت دینا شرط نہیں ہے یعنی کفالہ تنہا کفیل کے قول سے منعقد ہو جائے گا مکنول لا کا قبو کرنا شرط نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد کفالہ کفیل کا اپنے او پر مطالبہ کولازم کرنے کے تصرف کا نام ہے اور ہر وہ تصرف جس کو اپنے اوپر لازم کیا جائے اس میں لازم کرنے والا مستقل اور خود مختار ہوتا ہے اس میں دوسرے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی جیسے اقرار کرنے والاشی مقربہ کا اقرار کرنے میں مستقل ہوتا ہے۔ مقرلہ کے قبول کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی اور جیسے نذر کرنے 114 شی کمند دور کو اپنے اوپر لازم کرنے میں مستقل ہوتا ہے کسی کے قبول کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی اس طرح کھیل بھی اپنے اوپر مطالبہ اہ زمہ کرنے میں مستقل اور خود مختار ہو گا اس میں مکفول الیہ کے قبول کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہ ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف کی پہلی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد ایجاب اور قبول کے مجموعہ کا نام ہے لہذا عقد کفالہ میں بھی کفیل نے ایجاب کے بعد مکفول لد کا قبول کرنا ضروری ہوگا مگر چونکہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک خطر عقد یعنی قبول ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف ہو سکتا ہے جیسا کہ فضولی فی النکاح کے بیان میں اشرف الہدایہ جلد چہارم ص ۸۸ پر گذر چکا ہے اس لئے مکسول لہ کا قبول کرنا اور اجازات دینا بھی ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف ہوگا یعنی مکفول لن اگر عقد کفالہ کی مجلس کی اجازت دیدی تو کفالہ درست ہو جائے گا اور اگر اجازت ؟
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد کفالہ میں تملیک کے معنی موجود ہیں اس طور پر کہ عقد کفالہ کے ذریعہ کفیل ، مکفول لہ کو اپنے اوپر مطالبہ کا مالک کرتا ہے اور جس چیز میں تملیک کے معنی ہوں وہ مالک بنانے والے اور مالک بنے والے دونوں کے ساتھ قائم ہوتی ہے اک عقد کہا کہ نبیل اور مسطول الہ دونوں کے ساتھ قائم ہو گا جب معتقد کفالہ تیل اور ملٹول لہ دونوں کے ساتھ قائم ہے تو عقد کنالہ میں کٹیل کا ایجاب اور ماھوال ان کا قبول دونوں ضروری ہوں گے۔ حالانکہ صورت مذکورہ میں فقط نفیل کا ایجاب موجود ہے تو یہ ماورا مجلس پر موقوف نہ ہوگا کیونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک شطر عقد یعنی عقد کا ایک جز ما را مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اگر کنٹیل کے ایجاب کو کسی
Kafalah is not valid except with the acceptance of the creditor in the session. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: It is valid if (the creditor) is informed and then permits. In some copies, permission is not a condition. And the dispute applies to both kafalah for the person and for property. For him (Abu Yusuf), it is a commitment contract (tasarruf iltizami), so the one making the commitment is independent. This is the basis for this narration from him. And the reason for suspension (on permission) is what we mentioned regarding fuduli in marriage. For both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it contains the meaning of transfer of ownership (tamlik), i.e., transferring the right to claim, so it involves both parties. Only half the contract is present (the offer), so it cannot be suspended on what is beyond the session. Translation: And kafalah is not valid except with the acceptance of the creditor in the session, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: It is valid provided that when he is informed, he gives permission, and in some copies permission is not a condition. This dispute is in both kafalah for person and property. Abu Yusuf's evidence: The contract of kafalah is a commitment contract, so the one committing is independent. This is the basis for this narration. The reason for suspension on permission is what we mentioned regarding fuduli in marriage. The evidence of both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): Kafalah contains the meaning of ownership transfer, i.e., the kafil makes the creditor owner of the right to claim from him. Thus, this meaning involves both—the kafil and the creditor—and only half the contract (the offer) is present, so it is not suspended on what is beyond the session. Commentary: The case is that both in kafalah for property and for person, according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), a condition for validity is that the creditor accepts in the session. If he does not accept, kafalah is invalid. This is also a view of Imam Shafi'i. Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one that if the creditor is not present in the session, validity is suspended on his permission—if he permits in the session where he learns of the kafalah, it becomes valid; otherwise not. This is also the view of Malik, Ahmad, and one view of Shafi'i. The second narration: acceptance and permission are not conditions; kafalah is contracted solely by the kafil's statement. Evidence for second narration: Kafalah is a commitment (iltizam) that the kafil imposes on himself; in such commitments, the one imposing is independent, like in iqrar (acknowledgment) and nadhr (vow). Evidence for first narration: A contract is composed of offer and acceptance; so after the offer, acceptance by the creditor is necessary. But since according to Abu Yusuf, one part of the contract (acceptance) can be suspended on the future (like in fuduli marriage), the creditor's acceptance can be given later, and if he gives permission, it becomes valid. The evidence of the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): Kafalah contains the meaning of tamlik (transfer of ownership) of the right to claim. This meaning requires both the transferor (kafil) and the transferee (creditor) to be present, so offer and acceptance are both necessary. Since only the offer is present, it cannot be suspended on the future, because in their view, half the contract cannot be suspended.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the formation of the kafalah contract. The matn states that kafalah is not valid except with the acceptance (qabul) of the creditor (makful lahu) in the session (majlis). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: (1) kafalah is valid if the creditor, upon notification, gives permission (ijazah) even outside the session; (2) no acceptance is required at all—the guarantor's offer alone effects the contract. The dispute extends to both kafalah bi'l-mal (guarantee of debt) and kafalah bi'l-nafs (guarantee of person). Abu Yusuf's first view analogizes kafalah to the contract of a fuduli in marriage, which is suspended on acceptance. His second view considers kafalah a unilateral commitment (iltizam) like an acknowledgement (iqrar) or vow (nadhr). The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that kafalah involves a transfer of ownership (tamlik) of the right to claim, which requires both parties—offeror and acceptor—and therefore the acceptance must occur in the same session. They hold that only half the contract (the offer) is present, so it cannot be suspended on acceptance outside the session. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that acceptance in the session is required for validity, as stated explicitly by the matn.

Key Terms
قبول (qabul): The creditor's verbal acceptance of the surety in the session of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, when must the creditor accept the kafalah for it to be valid?
A) Within one month of the offer
B) In the same session as the offer
C) At any time before the debt is due
D) Acceptance is never required

Key Takeaway
The validity of kafalah in the Hanafi school hinges on the creditor's acceptance occurring in the same session as the offer; this requirement stems from the nature of kafalah as a bilateral contract involving transfer of ownership of the right to claim.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Creditor's Acceptance in Kafalah: Sahibayn vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on creditor's acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on creditor's acceptance in kafalah and explain the reasoning of the Sahibayn versus Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Kafalah requires creditor's acceptance in the same session because it involves tamlik (making an owner).

Kafalah (suretyship) is a contract where the surety becomes responsible for a debt or the presence of a person. A key intra-Hanafi dispute concerns whether the creditor's acceptance is necessary for validity. This lesson examines the views of the two masters (Sahibayn) and Imam Abu Yusuf, including the qiyas reasoning and the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions
State the three positions: Sahibayn require acceptance in the same session; Abu Yusuf's first narration requires acceptance in any session; Abu Yusuf's second narration requires no acceptance.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Understand that kafalah is a contract of tamlik (making the creditor owner of the right to demand), which requires both offer and acceptance in the same session because a part of the contract cannot be deferred.
Tamlik necessitates presence of both parties.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's second narration
This view considers kafalah as pure iltizam (binding oneself), akin to iqrar and nadhr, where the person acts independently and no acceptance is needed.
The qiyas is to iqrar and nadhr.
4
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's first narration
This view treats acceptance as necessary but allows it to be given in a later session, based on the permissibility of deferring a part of the contract as seen in fuduli marriage.
The analogy is to the unauthorized person in marriage.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Sahibayn: acceptance in the same session is a condition for validity, whether by the creditor or a representative (fuduli) with later ratification.
This is the position applied in fatwa.

طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد كفالہ میں تملیک کے معنی موجود ہیں اس طور پر کہ عقد كفالہ کے ذریعہ كفیل ، مكفول لہ کو اپنے اوپر مطالبہ کا مالک کرتا ہے اور جس چیز میں تملیک کے معنی ہوں وہ مالک بنانے والے اور مالک بنائے والے دونوں کے ساتھ قائم ہوتی ہے اس لئے عقد كفالہ كفیل اور مكفول لہ دونوں کے ساتھ قائم ہو گا جب عقد كفالہ كفیل اور مكفول لہ دونوں کے ساتھ قائم ہے تو عقد كفالہ میں كفیل کا ایجاب اور مكفول لہ کا قبول دونوں ضروری ہوں گے۔ حالانکہ صورت مذکورہ میں فقط كفیل کا ایجاب موجود ہے تو یہ ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہ ہوگا كیونكہ طرفین کے نزدیک شطر عقد یعنی عقد کا ایک جز ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اگر كفیل کے ایجاب کو كسی فضولی نے مكفول لہ کی طرف سے مجلس کے اندر قبول کرلیا پھر مكفول لہ کو خبر پہنچنے پر اجازت دے دی تو یہ بالاتفاق جائز ہے اور اگر مجلس میں کسی فضولی نے بھی قبول نہ كیا تو مكفول لہ کی اجازت كچھ کار آمد نہ ہوگی حاصل یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک كفالہ درست ہونے کے لئے ایجاب كفیل کے بعد اس مجلس میں قبول کرنا شرط ہے خواہ مكفول لہ قبول کرے یا اس کی طرف سے کوئی فضولی قبول کرے اور اگر فضولی نے قبول كیا ہو تو مكفول لہ کو خبر پہنچنے پر اس کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگا۔
Book of Suretyship. In both suretyship by person and suretyship by property, the proof of Abu Yusuf is that the contract of suretyship is a binding disposition, so the one undertaking it is independent in it, and this is the reason for that narration from Abu Yusuf, and the reason for being contingent upon the permission of the creditor is what we mentioned regarding the unauthorized person in marriage. And the proof of the two masters is that in the contract of suretyship, there is the meaning of making someone owner, and that is that the surety makes the creditor owner of the right to demand from him. So this meaning is established with both the surety and the creditor, and here the presence of one part does not make it contingent upon beyond the session. Explanation: The scenario is that whether it is suretyship by property or suretyship by person, according to the two masters, the condition for validity of suretyship is that the creditor accepts it in the session of suretyship. So if the creditor does not accept the suretyship in the session, the suretyship is not valid. This is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: One narration is that if the creditor is not present in the session of suretyship, then the permissibility of suretyship is contingent upon his permission, meaning that when the news of suretyship reaches the creditor in whatever session, if he gives permission in that session, the suretyship becomes valid, and if he does not give permission, the suretyship is not valid. Those who hold this view are Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and this is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. The second narration is that for suretyship to occur, acceptance by the creditor and giving permission are not conditions; i.e., suretyship is concluded by the word of the surety alone; acceptance by the creditor is not a condition. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf's second narration is that the contract of suretyship is the name for the surety's making the demand incumbent upon himself. And every disposition that is made incumbent upon oneself, the one who makes it incumbent is independent and autonomous; there is no need for another, like the one who makes a confession is independent in his confession; there is no need for the acceptance of the conferee, and like the one who makes a vow is independent in making the vow incumbent upon himself; there is no need for anyone's acceptance. Similarly, the surety is independent and autonomous in making the demand incumbent upon himself; there is little need for acceptance by the creditor. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf's first narration is that a contract is the name for the combination of offer and acceptance. Therefore, in the contract of suretyship as well, after the offer by the surety, acceptance by the creditor is necessary. However, since according to Imam Abu Yusuf a part of the contract, i.e., acceptance, can be contingent upon beyond the session, as mentioned in the discussion of the unauthorized person in marriage in Ashraf al-Hidayah volume 4 page 88, so acceptance and permission by the creditor can also be contingent upon beyond the session; i.e., if the creditor gives permission after the session of the suretyship contract, the suretyship becomes valid, and if he does not give permission, the suretyship is not valid. The proof of the two masters is that in the contract of suretyship, the meaning of making someone owner exists, in the sense that through the contract of suretyship, the surety makes the creditor owner of the right to demand from him. And a thing that has the meaning of making someone owner is established with both the one making ownership and the one being made owner. Therefore, the contract of suretyship is established with both the surety and the creditor. Since the contract of suretyship is established with both, both the offer of the surety and the acceptance of the creditor are necessary. But in the mentioned scenario, only the offer of the surety exists, so it is not contingent upon beyond the session, because according to the two masters, a part of the contract, i.e., a part of the contract, is not contingent upon beyond the session. However, it must be said that if some unauthorized person accepts the offer of the surety on behalf of the creditor within the session, then upon the news reaching the creditor and his giving permission, this is unanimously valid. And if no unauthorized person accepts in the session, then the permission of the creditor is of no effect. The conclusion is that according to the two masters, for suretyship to be valid, after the offer of the surety, acceptance in that session is a condition, whether the creditor accepts or some unauthorized person accepts on his behalf. And if an unauthorized person accepted, it is contingent upon the permission of the creditor upon being informed.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the requirement of the creditor's acceptance for the validity of a suretyship contract (kafalah). The author first presents the issue: In both kafalah bil-nafs (suretyship for the person) and kafalah bil-mal (suretyship for property), there is a difference between the two masters (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam Abu Yusuf himself (since he has two narrations). According to the two masters, acceptance by the creditor (makful lahu) in the same session (majlis) is a condition for validity. If the creditor does not accept, the contract is invalid. This is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i in one narration. Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: In the first, if the creditor is not present in the session, the contract's validity is contingent upon his permission later, but that permission must be given in a session where he hears the news. This view is shared by Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam al-Shafi'i in another narration. In the second narration, acceptance is not a condition at all; the contract is concluded solely by the surety's offer, analogous to confession (iqrar) and vow (nadhr), where the person acting independently does not need acceptance from anyone. The two masters rebut this by arguing that kafalah involves tamlik (making someone owner of a right), which inherently requires both parties: the surety makes the creditor owner of the right to demand, so both offer and acceptance are essential. Regarding the possibility of deferred acceptance, the two masters maintain that a part of the contract cannot be postponed beyond the session. However, they allow an exception: if a third party (fuduli) accepts on behalf of the creditor within the session, and later the creditor ratifies it, it is valid by consensus. If no one accepts in the session, the creditor's later permission is useless. Hence, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that acceptance in the same session is required, whether by the creditor directly or by a representative, with subsequent ratification only valid if a representative accepted in the session.

Key Terms
كفالة (Kafalah): A contract whereby a person (kafil) undertakes to be responsible for a debt or the presence of another person (makful 'anhu) before the creditor (makful lahu).
مكفول له (Makful lahu): The creditor or the person to whom the surety is given; the beneficiary of the kafalah contract.
طرفین (Tarafayn): The two masters: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn), what is required for a kafalah contract to be valid?
A) Only the surety's offer is needed; acceptance is not required.
B) The creditor must accept in the same session as the offer, either directly or through a representative.
C) The creditor may accept in any session after the offer.
D) Acceptance by any Muslim present is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires the creditor's acceptance in the same session for kafalah to be valid, based on the tamlik nature of the contract.

Kafalah — Surety

Exception to Acceptance: Sick Debtor's Kafalah by Heir
Explaining the exceptional case where kafalah is valid without creditor's acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exceptional case where kafalah is valid without the creditor's acceptance, explain the istihsan reasoning, and identify the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Kafalah by an heir at a sick debtor’s request is valid without creditor acceptance because it is treated as a will (wasiyyah) by istihsan.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that kafalah (suretyship) requires the creditor's acceptance in the same session. However, there is one well-known exception: when a sick debtor (marid) tells his heir to become surety for his debt, the kafalah is valid even if the creditors are absent and do not accept. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this exception, which is based on istihsan (juristic preference), and clarifies the conditions under which it applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and the exception
Recall that the general rule (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) requires the creditor's acceptance in the session for kafalah to be valid. The exception is when a sick debtor says to his heir, 'Become surety for me for the debt that is upon me,' and the heir agrees, without the creditors present.
The exception is limited to the specific wording and parties.
2
Understand the qiyas that would invalidate it
By strict analogy (qiyas), this kafalah would be invalid because the creditor is absent and has not accepted. The same situation with a healthy debtor or a stranger would be invalid.
Qiyas alone leads to invalidity.
3
Grasp the istihsan reasoning
The Hanafi scholars depart from qiyas using istihsan. They treat the sick debtor's statement as a will (wasiyyah) directing the heir to pay off debts. Since the purpose is to free the debtor's liability, and the creditor benefits, the requirement of acceptance is dropped. The situation is likened to a command for marriage (amr bil-nikah), which also does not require acceptance.
The key is the interpretation as a will.
4
Note the conditions and the ikhtilaf
The exception applies only when the sick debtor has wealth (to make the will meaningful), the heir is the addressee, and the wording is explicit. If the debtor says this to a stranger, there is disagreement among the scholars (mashayikh).
The exception is not a general relaxation; it has specific conditions.

قال الا في مسئلة واحدة و هى أن يقول المريض لوارثه تكفّل عنى بما على من الدين فكفل به مع عـ الغرماء جاز لأن ذالك وصية فى الحقيقة ولهذا تصح و ان لم يسم المكفول لهم ولهذا قالوا انما تصح اذا كان له مال او يقال أنه قائم مقام الطالب لحاجته اليه تفريغاً لذمته وفيه نفع الطالب كما اذا حضر بنفسه وانما يصح بهذا اللفظ ولا يشترط القبول لأنه يراد به التحقيق دون المساومة ظاهرا في هذه الحالة فصار كالأمر بالنكاح ولو قال المريض ذالك لأجنبي اختلف المشائخ فيه
ترجمہ سوائے ایک مسئلہ کے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مریض اپنے وارث سے کہے کہ تو میری طرف سے اس قرضہ کا كفیل ہو جا جو مجھ پر ہے پس وہ قرض خواہوں کی عدم موجودگی کے باوجود اس کا كفیل ہو گیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ حقيقت میں وصیت ہے اور اسی وجہ سے كفالہ صحیح ہوتا ہے اگر چہ مكفول لہ جو لوگ ہیں ان کا نام بھی نہ لیا ہو، اور اسی وجہ سے مشائخ نے کہا کہ یہ كفالہ اس وقت صحیح ہوگا جبکہ مریض کے پاس مال ہو یا یوں کہا جائے گا کہ مریض ، طالب، ( قرض خواہ ) کے قائم مقام ہے کیونکہ مریض کو اس بات کی ضرورت ہے کہ اس کا ذمہ فارغ ہو اور اس میں طالب کا نفع ہے جیسے اگر طالب خود حاضر ہوتا اور اس لفظ سے كفالہ کا صحیح ہونا اور قبول کا شرط نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ اس سے مراد تحقیق ہے نہ کہ اس حالت میں ظاہری طور پر معاملہ چکانا ۔ پس یہ امر بالنكاح کے مانند ہو گیا اور اگر مریض نے یہ بات کسی اجنبی سے کہی تو اس میں مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے۔
تشریح سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک مكفول لہ کے قبول کئے بغیر كفالہ صحیح نہیں ہوتا مگر ایک مسئلہ ایسا ہے جس میں حتی كفالہ کے لئے طرفین کے نزدیک بھی مكفول کا مجلس کے اندر قبول کرنا شرط نہیں ہے اور وہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مریض قرضدار نے اپنے وارث سے کہا کہ تو میری طرف سے اس قرضہ کا كفیل ہو جا جو مجھ پر واجب ہے پس وارث اس کی طرف سے اس قرضہ کا كفیل ہو گیا حالانکہ قرض خواہ موجود نہیں ہیں تو یہ كفالہ استحسانا جائز ہے اگر چہ قیاسا جائز نہیں ہے وجہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ یہاں بھی مكفول لہ غائب ہے اور مكفول لہ کے مجلس میں قبول كئے بغیر كفالہ درست نہ ہوگا اور اس لئے کہ اگر تندرست آدمی اپنے ورثہ سے قرض خواہوں کی عدم موجودگی میں تكفل عنى بما على من الدین کہتا اور وہ كفیل ہو جاتے یا کسی اجنبی سے کہتا اور وہ كفیل ہو جاتا تو یہ كفالہ درست نہ ہوتا پس اسی طرح "الا في مسألة واحدة" میں بھی كفالہ درست نہ ہوگا۔
وجہ استحسان دو ہیں ایک یہ کہ مریض مدیون کا قول تكفل عنى بما على من الدين وصیت کے معنی میں ہے یعنی تكفل عنی کا مطلب ہے اقضوا ديونی میرے دیون ادا کر دو اور جب ورثہ نے تكفلنا بھا کہا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے کہا کہ ہم تیرا تمام قرض ادا کر دیں گے۔
He said: Except for one issue, and that is when a sick person says to his heir, 'Become surety for me for the debt that is upon me,' so he becomes surety for it in the absence of the creditors, it is valid because that is in reality a will (wasiyyah), and for this reason it is valid even if he did not name the creditors. And for this reason they said that it is only valid if he has wealth, or it is said that he (the sick person) stands in the place of the claimant due to his need to free his liability, and in that there is benefit for the claimant, just as if he himself had been present. And it is only valid with this wording, and acceptance is not a condition because what is intended is actualization (tahqiq) and not bargaining, apparently in this situation. So it became like the command for marriage. And if the sick person said that to a stranger, the scholars differed in it.
Translation: Except for one issue, and that is when a sick debtor says to his heir, 'Become surety for me for this debt that is upon me,' then he became surety for it despite the absence of the creditors, so it is valid because this is in reality a will, and for this reason the suretyship is valid even if he did not name the creditors. And for this reason the scholars said that this suretyship will be valid only when the sick person has wealth, or it will be said that the sick person stands in the place of the claimant because the sick person needs his liability to be freed, and in that there is benefit for the claimant, like if the claimant himself were present. And the validity of suretyship with this wording and the non-conditionality of acceptance is because what is intended is actualization, not outward settlement in this situation. So it became like the command for marriage. And if the sick person said that to a stranger, the scholars differed in it.
Explanation: It has passed previously that according to the two masters, without the acceptance of the creditor, the suretyship is not valid. But there is one issue such that even for suretyship, according to the two masters, acceptance by the creditor in the session is not a condition. And that issue is that a sick debtor said to his heir, 'Become surety for me for this debt that is obligatory upon me,' then the heir became surety for this debt on his behalf while the creditors are not present, so this suretyship is valid by istihsan, although by qiyas it is not valid. The reason for qiyas is that here too the creditor is absent, and without the acceptance of the creditor in the session, the suretyship is not valid, and because if a healthy person said to his heirs in the absence of creditors, 'Become surety for me for what is upon me of debt,' and they became surety, or if he said to a stranger and he became surety, this suretyship would not be valid. So similarly in 'except for one issue' as well, the suretyship would not be valid. The reason for istihsan is two: One is that the statement of the sick debtor 'takaffal 'anni bima 'alayya min al-dayn' is in the meaning of a will, i.e., 'takaffal 'anni' means 'pay my debts'. And when the heirs said 'takaffalna', its meaning is that they said, 'We will pay all your debt.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage discusses an exceptional case in the chapter of kafalah. The general rule (according to the two masters) is that kafalah requires the creditor's acceptance in the same session. However, there is one exception: when a sick debtor (marid) says to his heir, 'Become surety for me for the debt that is upon me,' and the heir accepts, the kafalah is valid even though the creditors are not present and no acceptance occurs. This is an istihsan (juridical preference) ruling, contrary to qiyas which would invalidate it. The author explains that this statement is treated as a will (wasiyyah) in reality, because the sick person is essentially asking his heirs to pay off his debts. Since the intention is to free the debtor's liability, and the creditor benefits from this as well, the requirement of acceptance is dropped. The heir's acceptance is not needed because the situation 'tabiqiq' (actualization) rather than 'musawamah' (bargaining). It is likened to an order for marriage (amr bil-nikah), which also does not require acceptance to be effective. The exception is conditional: the sick person must have wealth (to make the will meaningful), and the wording must be explicit. If the sick person says this to a stranger (not an heir), the scholars differ; there is no consensus. The text highlights that the basis of the exception is istihsan, which overrides the qiyas that would require acceptance.

Key Terms
استحسان (Istihsan): A method of juristic preference that allows departing from strict qiyas for reasons of necessity, custom, or public interest. Here, it overrides the qiyas requiring creditor acceptance.
وصية (Wasiyyah): A will or bequest. In this context, the sick debtor's request to his heir is interpreted as a will directing the heir to pay the debts.
مريض (Marid): A sick person, especially one whose illness is terminal (marad al-mawt) such that his actions are treated with the rules of wills and bequests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the creditor is assumed to consent.
B) Because the statement is treated as a will (wasiyyah) to pay off debts.
C) Because the heir has authority over the debtor's estate.
D) Because the creditor's acceptance is never required in kafalah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds an exceptional kafalah by an heir at a sick debtor's request, validated by istihsan as akin to a will, despite the absence of creditor acceptance.

Exception in Kafalah: Sick Debtor's Guarantee by Heir as a Will
Explains the exception where a sick debtor's guarantee by heir is valid without creditor's acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exception where a sick debtor's instruction to his heir to guarantee his debt is valid without the creditor's acceptance, and explain the two istihsan bases for this ruling.

Core Idea
A sick debtor's instruction to his heir is treated as a will, so the creditor's acceptance is not required.

In Hanafi fiqh, a valid kafalah normally requires the creditor's acceptance in the same session as the guarantor's offer. However, there is a notable exception: when a person on his deathbed tells his heir to guarantee his debts. This passage from the Hidayah explains why this exceptional ruling is justified by istihsan (juristic preference), treating the kafalah as a will (wasiyyah) rather than a standard suretyship. Understanding this exception is crucial for properly applying the rules of kafalah in delicate situations involving death and debt.

Guided Path
1
Restate the general rule
Recall that the Hanafi school requires offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) in the same session for a valid kafalah, as mentioned in the beginning of the passage.
This applies to both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
Identify the exception
Focus on the phrase 'except in one case' (illa fi mas'ala wahida). The exception occurs when a sick debtor says to his heir 'Takaffal `anni bima `alayya min al-dayn' (Guarantee for me what I owe of debt), and the heir agrees, even in the absence of the creditors.
The exception is specific to this wording and context.
3
Explain the qiyas reasoning
Understand why by qiyas this kafalah would be invalid: the absence of creditor's acceptance is present, just like in ordinary cases, so it should be invalid. This highlights the need for istihsan.
Qiyas here is straightforward and would negate validity.
4
Unpack the two istihsan arguments
The passage gives two reasons for the exception: (a) The debtor's words are tantamount to a will (wasiyyah), which does not require acceptance from beneficiaries. (b) The debtor stands in the place of the creditor due to his need to clear his liability, and the creditor benefits, making it as if the creditor himself accepted.
Both arguments override qiyas.
5
Note additional conditions and ikhtilaf
The text mentions that this ruling applies only when the debtor has wealth at death; otherwise, the guarantee is not binding. Also, if the sick debtor says this to a non-heir (ajnabi), the mashayikh differed. Acknowledge the ikhtilaf.
This shows the nuance within the madhhab.

كتاب الكفاله
اشرف البدایہ جلد تم فضولی نے مکغول لیا کی طرف سے مجلس کے اندر قبول کرلیا پھر مکفول این خبر پہنچنے پر اجازت دیدی تو یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے اور اگر مجلس میں کسی فضولی نے بھی قبول نہ کیا تو مکفول لہ کی اجازت کچھ کار آمد نہ ہوگی حاصل یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک کفالہ درست ہونے کے لئے ایجاب کفیل کے بعد اس مجلس میں قبول کرنا شرط ہے خواہ مکفول لہ قبول کرے یا اس کی طرف سے کوئی فضولی قبول کرے اور اگر فضولی نے قبول کیا ہو تو مکفول لا کو خبر پہنچنے پر اس کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگا۔
